id="top"></a>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n\t\t\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of retired Australian cyclone names</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">\n\t\t\t\t\tJump to:\t\t\t\t\t<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, \t\t\t\t\t<a href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg/220px-Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg/330px-Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg/440px-Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5100" data-file-height="4500" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monica_2006-04-24_0139Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSatellite image of <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Monica" title="Cyclone Monica">Cyclone Monica</a>, the strongest recorded tropical cyclone in the Australian region by wind speed</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">Tropical cyclones</a> are non-<a href="/wiki/Weather_front" title="Weather front">frontal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low pressure systems</a> that develop, within an environment of warm <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> and little vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> aloft.<sup id="cite_ref-SPAC_TCOP_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPAC_TCOP-1">[1]</a></sup> Within the Australian region, names are assigned from three <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_names#Australian_Region_.2890.C2.B0E_-_160.C2.B0E.29" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical cyclone names">pre-determined lists</a>, to such systems, once they reach or exceed ten\xe2\x80\x93minute <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">sustained wind speeds</a> of 65&#160;km/h (40&#160;mph), near the center, by either the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Meteorology" title="Bureau of Meteorology">Bureau of Meteorology</a> or by the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Warning_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Cyclone Warning Center">Tropical Cyclone Warning Centers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jakarta,_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Jakarta, Indonesia">Jakarta, Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby,_Papua_New_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Moresby, Papua New Guinea">Port Moresby, Papua New Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SPAC_TCOP_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPAC_TCOP-1">[1]</a></sup> Within the Australian region, tropical cyclones have been <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">officially named</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Pre-1970_Southern_Hemisphere_tropical_cyclone_seasons#1960.E2.80.9361_to_1968.E2.80.9369_cyclone_seasons" title="Pre-1970 Southern Hemisphere tropical cyclone seasons">1963\xe2\x80\x9364 Australian region cyclone season</a>, though several meteorological papers show that a few tropical cyclones were named before 1964\xe2\x80\x9365.<sup id="cite_ref-SPAC_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPAC-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vanuatu_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanuatu-4">[4]</a></sup> The names of significant tropical cyclones that cause a high amount of damage and/or loss of life are retired from the lists of tropical cyclone names by either the Bureau of Meteorology or the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>\'s RA&#160;V Tropical Cyclone Committee at their bi-annual meeting. Storms named by Port Moresby are automatically retired regardless of their impact due to their infrequent occurrence.<sup id="cite_ref-SPAC_TCOP_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPAC_TCOP-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Within the Australian region, there have been a total of 113&#160;tropical cyclone names retired, with the 1990s accounting for 44 of these. Two of the most intense systems ever recorded in the Southern Hemisphere, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Gwenda" title="Cyclone Gwenda">Cyclones Gwenda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Inigo" title="Cyclone Inigo">Inigo</a> each attaining a <a href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> of 900&#160;hPa (26.58&#160;inHg), are among the retired storms. The deadliest cyclone to take place since the 1960s was Cyclone Guba in 2007 which killed 149 people in Papua New Guinea. Additionally, the most damaging system was <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Tracy" title="Cyclone Tracy">Severe Tropical Cyclone Tracy</a> in 1974 which devastated the city of <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory" title="Darwin, Northern Territory">Darwin</a>, leaving A$837&#160;million (A$5.65&#160;billion 2011&#160;AUD; US$2.64&#160;billion 2011&#160;USD) in losses.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Background"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Background</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_1960s"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1960s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_1970s"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1970s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_1980s"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1980s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_1990s"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1990s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_2000s"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 2000s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_2010s"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 2010s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_retired_Australian_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historical_tropical_cyclone_names" class="mw-redirect" title="List of historical tropical cyclone names">List of historical tropical cyclone names</a></div>\n<p>Within the region the credit for the first usage of personal names for weather systems, is generally given to the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Queensland Government">Queensland Government</a> Meteorologist <a href="/wiki/Clement_Wragge" class="mw-redirect" title="Clement Wragge">Clement Wragge</a>, who named systems between 1887 - 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-5">[5]</a></sup> Wragge used names drawn from the letters of the Greek alphabet, Greek and Roman mythology and female names, to describe weather systems including tropical cyclones over <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-5">[5]</a></sup> After the new <a href="/wiki/Australian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian government">Australian government</a> had failed to create a federal weather bureau and appoint him director, Wragge started naming cyclones after political figures.<sup id="cite_ref-TC_FAQ_B1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TC_FAQ_B1-6">[6]</a></sup> This system of naming weather systems subsequently fell into disuse for several years after Wragge retired, before the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Bureau_of_Meteorology" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Bureau of Meteorology">Australian Bureau of Meteorology</a> started to use female names for tropical cyclones in the region during the <a href="/wiki/1963-64_Australian_region_cyclone_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1963-64 Australian region cyclone season">1963-64 cyclone season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During the International Women\'s Year of 1975 the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Innovation,_Industry,_Science_and_Research_(Australia)#List_of_science_ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Innovation, Industry, Science and Research (Australia)">Australian Science Minister</a> ordered that tropical cyclones, within the Australian region should carry both men\'s and women\'s names.<sup id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-5">[5]</a></sup> This was because the minister thought "that both sexes should bear the odium of the devastation caused by cyclones."<sup id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-5">[5]</a></sup> As a result, male names were added to the lists of names for both basins, ahead of the 1975-76 season.<sup id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The practice of retiring significant names was started during 1955 by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Weather_Bureau" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Weather Bureau">United States Weather Bureau</a> in the Northern Atlantic basin, after hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carol" title="Hurricane Carol">Carol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Edna" title="Hurricane Edna">Edna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">Hazel</a> struck the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeastern United States</a> and caused a significant amount of damage in the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahina_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahina-8">[8]</a></sup> Initially the names were only designed to be retired for ten years after which they might be reintroduced, however, it was decided at the 1969 Interdepartmental hurricane conference, that any significant hurricane in the future would have its name permanently retired.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahina_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahina-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Anna_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anna-9">[9]</a></sup> Several names have been removed from the Pacific naming lists for various other reasons than causing a significant amount of death/destruction, which include being pronounced in a very similar way to other names and political reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-WMO_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMO-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRD_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRD-11">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_1960s">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_retired_Australian_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>There were 3 tropical cyclone names retired during the 1960s, after the naming of tropical cyclones had restarted during the 1963-64 tropical cyclone season.<sup id="cite_ref-WMO_TCOP_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_TCOP-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="margin:auto">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Name</th>\n<th scope="col">Dates active</th>\n<th scope="col"><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">Peak classification</a></th>\n<th scope="col">Sustained<br />\nwind speeds</th>\n<th scope="col">Pressure</th>\n<th scope="col" class="unsortable">Areas affected</th>\n<th scope="col">Damages<br />\n(AUD)</th>\n<th scope="col">Damages<br />\n<small>(USD)</small></th>\n<th scope="col">Deaths</th>\n<th bgcolor="#CCFFFF">Category 2 tropical cyclone</td>\n<td><span style="display:none;" class="sortkey">100 !</span><span class="sorttext">Not Specified</span></td>\n<td>983&#160;hPa (29.03&#160;inHg)</td>\n<td>Northern Territory, Queensland</td>\n<td>Extensive</td>\n<td>Extensive</td>\n<td>None</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Audrey1964_14-0" class="reference"><a Queensland</td>\n<td>Extensive</td>\n<td>Extensive</td>\n<td>None</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Flora1964_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flora1964-15">[15]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Dinah</td>\n<td><span style="display:none;" class="sortkey">670122 !</span><span class="sorttext">22&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 31 January (27.91&#160;inHg)</td>\n<td>Queensland</td>\n<td>Severe</td>\n<td>Severe</td>\n<td>None</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="sortbottom">\n<th>3 names</th>\n<th colspan="5"><sup id="cite_ref-Retired_Names_Ref_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retired_Names_Ref-18">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity-21">[nb 2]</a></sup></th>\n<th>Extensive</th>\n<th>Extensive</th>\n<th>None</th>\n<th></th>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_1970s">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_retired_Australian_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>During the 1970s, 18 tropical cyclones had their names retired.<sup id="cite_ref-Retired_Names_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retired_Names-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> During this period, one of the most well-known storms in Australian history, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Tracy" title="Cyclone Tracy">Cyclone Tracy</a>, took place. It was both the costliest and deadliest of the decade; it would remain the costliest Australian cyclone until 2011 when <a href="/wiki/Severe_Tropical_Cyclone_Yasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Severe Tropical Cyclone Yasi">Severe Tropical Cyclone Yasi</a> surpassed it. A total of 87 people were killed between these storms and A$977&#160;million was wrought in damage.</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="margin:auto">\n<tr>\n<th href="#cite_note-JohnVanceDamage-92">[88]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="sortbottom">\n<th></th>\n<th colspan="5"><sup id="cite_ref-Retired_Names_Ref_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retired_Names_Ref-18">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity-21">[nb 2]</a></sup></th>\n<th></th>\n<th></th>\n<th></th>\n<th></th>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_2000s">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_retired_Australian_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png/220px-Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png/330px-Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png/440px-Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="633" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2000s.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTracks of storms retired in the 2000s</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>During the 2000s, 23 tropical cyclone names were retired. At the start of the 2008-09 season two sets of Indonesian names were established for the newly established TCWC Jakarta, while the naming lists for the three Australian TCWC\'s were combined. The name Hamish subsequently became the first name to be retired from these lists, after it impacted the coast of Queensland during 2008-09. The name Laurence was retired after it intensified into a category 5 severe tropical cyclone twice during December 2009 and affected Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-Laurence_93-0" style="display:none;" class="sortkey">925 !</span><span class="sorttext">925&#160;hPa (27.31&#160;inHg)</span></td>\n<td>Australia</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7007100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>$10&#160;million</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7006889670000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>$8.9&#160;million</td>\n<td><span id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="sortbottom">\n<th>23&#160;names</th>\n<th colspan="5"><sup id="cite_ref-Retired_Names_Ref_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retired_Names_Ref-18">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity-21">[nb 2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-08-10_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08-10-104">[nb 5]</a></sup></th>\n<th></th>\n<th></th>\n<th></th>\n<th></th>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Cyclone_names_retired_in_the_2010s">Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_retired_Australian_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Cyclone names retired in the 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png/220px-Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png/330px-Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png/440px-Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Retired_Australian_cyclone_tracks_2010s.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTracks of all storms retired in the 2010s</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>During the 2010s, ten names have been retired, because of impacts caused to either Australia or various South Pacific island nations including the Solomon Islands, New Caledonia and Tonga. At the start of the decade the name Magda was retired, after it made landfall on the Kimberley region of Western Australia, as a category 3 severe tropical cyclone.<sup id="cite_ref-Magda_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Magda-105">[100]</a></sup> The name Carlos was subsequently retired after it broke several rainfall records, as it impacted Darwin and North-Western Australia during February 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Carlos_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carlos-106">[101]</a></sup> The names Heidi and Lua were retired after the 2011-12 season and both had impacted the Pilbara region of Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-Heidi_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heidi-107">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lua_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lua-108">[103]</a></sup> The name Jasmine was also retired after the 2011-12 season and had affected the island nations of Vanuatu, New Caledonia and Tonga.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="margin:auto">\n<tr>\n<th
